B000OQF6N6|4.0|Zeitgeist has received a lot of flak since it was released, most of the criticism being drawn from the fact that neither D'arcy or James Iha appear on the album. A lot of people question whether this is a true Pumpkins album - I can tell you for sure that yes, Zeitgeist is a Smashing Pumpkins album.<br /><br />Billy Corgan is, has been and always will be The Smashing Pumpkins. Whilst Jimmy Chamberlin definitely has some amazing chemistry with Billy, 98% of the actual music and songwriting is entirely Billy. He has a right to the Smashing Pumpkins name, whether you like Zeitgeist or not.<br /><br />I see this album as a very straightforward statement by Billy - he can still rock. After Adore, Machina, Zwan and TheFutureEmbrace, I think fans were really calling for a rock album again. And thus, for Zeitgeist, Billy does away with the electronica elements that influened his latter day Pumpkins work and his solo album, and instead dusted off the strat, cranked up the distortion on his Marshall and Big Muff and decided to show us what alternative rock is again.<br /><br />Does it have the depth or range of Siamese Dream? No. Does it have the ambition of Gish? Probably not. Is it anywhere near as grand as Mellon Collie? Definitely not. But it never tries to be. That's what people fail to see, and that is why people are disappointed. After 7-years without The Smashing Pumpkins, fans expected Billy to produce another epic masterpiece straight away. Zeitgeist is a reintroduction, a moodsetter to remind fans that Billy still has more music to share with us.<br /><br />The actual album itself has its highs and lows. Songs like Starz, 7 Shades of Black, Come On (Let's Go) and the opening track, Doomsday Clock, are straight forward hard rock songs. Perhaps they don't have strong meanings behind them, but these songs are all about the music, and I believe cater much more to a live setting. I saw the Pumpkins live back in '08 when they were still touring on a lot of Zeitgeist tracks, and whilst something like Come On (Let's Go) sounds like a silly meaningless rock song in its recorded format, I received it completely different live.<br /><br />Bleeding the Orchid is an eerie ballad that helps give the album more substance and depth as Billy seems to experiment a bit more vocally and with production. Other tracks like Bring the Light and Tarantula (the lead single) really drive the album with catchy riffs and choruses that stick in the back of your mind well after you've finished listening.<br /><br />That's the Way, Neverlost and For God and Country make up the slower and calmer sections of the album. That's the Way is still a very poppy song and seems almost made for radio play, whilst For God and Country is an odd song that's uncharacteristic of Billy. Extremely heavy and overpowering bass backs the song as Billy righteously claims that he wants to fight for God and Country in a very restrained goth-pop track that seems to have an undertone of cynical patriotism, but I'm probably wrong there.<br />Neverlost seems like an underrated treasure on the album, a well written song that uses the classic Pumpkins formula of quiet verses and harder choruses.<br /><br />Zeitgeist's wild card though, is without a doubt, United States. The ten-minute progessive rock epic features some of the greatest drumming I have ever heard put to CD, and I would go as far as calling it Jimmy's magnum opus. United States is a definite mood setter, painting a dreary picture of the current state of America and the world in general. Billy's guitar work is simple for this track, yet very heavy and to the point. Halfway through, we're treated to a very creepy and distorted guitar piec until Jimmy and Billy explode back into the song with a fast hard rock beat.<br /><br />The album ends with Pomp and Circumstances, an odd song which won't end up on my list of favourite Pumpkins songs anytime soon, but it serves its purpose in ending Zeitgeist.<br /><br />I believe that Zeitgeist will actually end up being more like Adore and Machina in the way that it will be appreciated more in the future. Already (5 years on) people seem to be less resentful towards it. As time goes on, it wouldn't surprise me if people begin to consider Zeitgeist as a strong rock album, which is what it is. It doesn't have any serious range or depth, but in terms of rock albums, it's one of the better releases we've seen in the alternative market over the last few years. Jimmy also provides some of the best drumming of his career, whilst Billy continues to prove that he is one of the most underrated guitarists in the business today.<br />Stand out tracks go to Tarantula, United States and Bleeding the Orchid. It is worth at least one listen to help you make up your mind. Even the most avid Billy Corgan hater should be able to find at least one song to enjoy on this LP.

He starts with ancient times, when an excellent internal memory was necessary, when ancient books were very scarce.  Today, the ability to recite large amounts of material, without book-in-hand, is routine for actors on the stage, but for few other occasions.  For most of us, written lists and Google substitute for our relatively untrained memory.  Clearly most people can improve their memory by certain methods and practice. Foer describes some methods that rely on purposeful exaggeration to augment memory, by making things more exciting. Who are these survivors and will they maintain sanity or slowly slide into the abyss of madness.  This concept is played over and over and things get only worse as time passes.  I don't wish to give any more away.  We know that the world around them is in ruin but the reality of their situation is too much for them to mentally grasp and as the tension builds so does the danger and despair.  The walls of humanity shake and crumble and the images will haunt you long after the last scene.<br /><br />We know what is happening and yet the story continues to suck you in. B0059XTUVI|2.0|\\"The Iron Lady\\" is not the movie you expect it to be, nor is the movie you want it to be. That in it's self is not necessarily a bad thing, the reason that this is a bad movie is because what it is isn't very good. This is perhaps the least focused, least interesting biopic in a great many years. Considering it's fascinating subject, weather you agree politically or not, you've got to admit Marget Thatcher is an interesting woman and historical figure. What we get instead is a banal Lifetimeish movie of the week, a tear jerker, if you will, that no one cries over.<br /><br />\\"The Iron Lady\\" gives no insight into Mrs. Thatcher, little or no historical references, little in way of her personal life. Instead, the film seems focused on her weening years as she enters dementia and caries on conversations with her deceased husband. The unfocused script barely touched on issues of politics, how her gender affected her place in parliament or much of her personal sacrifices, that she must have made when ascending to the highest office in the land. This is the kind of vague biography where the subject is kept continuously at arms length. I have read that those who support this movie claim that it is well made, I disagree, it may look professionally made, but the film is undermined by flashbacks, edits and montages that keep the viewer disorientated.<br /><br />Much has been said of Meryl Streep's performance as Mrs. Thatcher, well it is interesting and it is good, but not in the way most think it is. There is so little insight into Thatcher's personality and no emotional depth, that Streep is left to do little more than mimic her voice, her mannerisams, and thanks to a fine make-up specialist, her appearance. This isn't a performance so much, as an impersonation, a good one indeed, but an impersonation no less. Was Streep worth of the Best Actress Oscar? I don't really think so, an Academy Award should be seen as a standard of excellence, but in all facets of life mistakes are made, and the academy has made more than their fair share over the years.<br /><br />\\"The Iron Lady\\" was directed by Phyllida Lloyd, from a screenplay by Abi Morgan, who is a highly respected theatre director, her previous film was \\"Mama Mia!\\". I have read that miss Lloyd believes Thatcher to have been the most important woman in politics since Elizabeth 1. A valid point of view, not shared by all, but with such a strong belief in her subject, I have to ask, why did she so willingly let her down. A better focused, more interesting, and possibly better acted, movie will some day be made about Margret Thatcher. Until then, it's still best to get your history, even recent history for a good book.

B006OB3K56|5.0|This is the story of two struggling people: sex addict Brandon and his emotionally dependent sister Sissy.  When the latter shows up out of the blue (well, after leaving countless distressing messages on Brandon's answering machine), the pair must cope with their own messed up lives.  And, like most people, they don't cope very well at all.<br /><br />There isn't much plot in SHAME.  It's a slow-moving character study.  It's also not for everyone.  The NC-17 rating isn't much for the content (we've seen more graphic stuff in R-rated films), but for the way the content is handled: unflinchingly, without judgement, without condemnation, and perhaps with a tad bit of understanding.  Director/writer Steve McQueen makes frequent use of extended shots; this adds and aura of unease to even the film's more beautiful moments (a real-time take of Carey Mulligan singing \\"New York, New York\\" is most memorable).  The script is intelligent, and never belittles its characters; nor does it put them up on some pedestal of victimhood and pity.  It's simply an honest take on two incredibly realistic individuals.<br /><br />None of that would be possible, of course, without the right actors.  Thankfully, both Michael Fassbender and Carey Mulligan have proven themselves worthy of the job.  They deliver their best performances here; the bravery isn't necessarily in their willingness to bare it all before the camera, but in the off-handed way they do so.  The relationship between Brandon and Sissy is incredibly strained and at times uncomfortable; Fassbender and Mulligan don't shy away from this, but instead embrace it and swing for the fences.  These are truly award-worthy performances; the film's edgy content may have scares away the Academy Awards, but actors of this caliber don't really care.  There will be awards for Fassbender and Mulligan some day.  Right now, they give gripping, memorable performances in a film that is a must-see for anyone who appreciates quality filmmaking, and isn't afraid of stepping outside their emotional comfort zone.isn't afraid of stepping outside their emotional comfort zone.

0061785652|1.0|All I can say for Mr. Rollins fan base is that they are not a very discriminating group. I have read several of his books through the past few years, and found them so poorly researched that I hadn't read one for over two years. When I saw The Devil Colony at my library, the premise of the book sounded interesting enough that I thought I would give him another try.<br /><br />Big mistake. The author is still writing about a secret agency - Sigma - which is populated by former Special Forces operatives and DARPA scientists, but the author still doesn't know the difference between a revolver and a semi-automatic pistol. In one scene, Hank Kanosh empties his Ruger Blackhawk at the bad guys in a helicopter until his \\"clip\\" runs out. Ruger Blackhawks are single action revolvers (Western style \\"sixguns\\" for those who don't know what a single action revolver is), and they don't use \\"clips\\" (magazines: the detachable metal piece that is loaded with cartridges - not \\"bullets\\" - and inserted into the pistol, usually into the grip of the handgun, as with the Glock pistols used so often in the movies these days). While it is certainly authentic that a guy who travels in the West, and sometimes on horseback, might choose to carry a revolver that has to be cocked by hand for every shot and only holds six cartridges, Mr. Rollins should definitely have known the gun does not use a \\"clip\\".<br /><br />Later, one of his characters is in a helicopter that is caught in extreme turbulence due to an explosion (volcanic, IIRC), and joins the pilot in \\"hauling back\\" on the cyclic control to prevent the aircraft from crashing.<br /><br />As a helicopter pilot who has flown through extreme turbulence (once while crossing Military Pass on the east side of Mt. Shasta in Northern California under a rotor cloud concealed by a cumulus formation) I can tell you that the cyclic control neither requires - nor benefits from - having two people pull on it. A six year old child can pull hard enough to operate the cyclic throughout its entire range of movement, even in turbulence.<br /><br />There were other ridiculous errors in information that showed how poorly Rollins researches his novels, an issue I had with the others I had read. In addition, his characters - so \\"highly trained\\" in Special Forces operations, etc., made some of the most ignorant and silly mistakes imaginable. I'm sure they were simply a plot device to enable Mr. Rollins to have them demonstrate ingenuity in getting out of the \\"fix\\" they found themselves in, but it was completely unbelievable and made the novel painful to read.<br /><br />I'm glad there are people who can enjoy such poor writing, if only because it is nice that they can enjoy themselves, and nice that Mr. Rollins can make a few bucks (far more than his books deserve, IMHO), but if you prefer any sort of believable action and accuracy in your stories, avoid this author like the Plague.perate the cyclic throughout its entire range of movement, even in turbulence.<br /><br />There were other ridiculous errors in information that showed how poorly Rollins researches his novels, an issue I had with the others I had read. B006RUJST6|5.0|It is always an amazing book that immediately drives me to get up and DO. I don't just finish the book and reflect on the things I have read. I have an overwhelming desire to change something in my life or do something that I have never done before. I find myself wanting to truly experience something, to go out and LIVE life to its fullest. That is what Slammed did to me. No, nothing really life changing occurred with me after reading this book, but I couldn't move on until I immediately loaded the Avett Brothers onto my Pandora playlist so I could hear their amazing music. Then I searched for the beautiful lyrics of their songs so that I could soak them in and interpret them for myself. I have a need to find somewhere, anywhere within driving distance for me to see Slam poetry in action. I found myself sitting in my spare moments and thinking about the Slam poetry that I could perform about the moments in my life that have impacted me the most. I don't just want to sit around and think about the things that I read about in this novel. I want to DO.<br /><br />In short, this is a book about grieving, but ultimately this is a book about living. Lake (a strange name for a main character, but soon it becomes natural and right to me as a name once I got to know her) finds herself transplanted from Texas to Michigan when her mom and she, along with a younger brother, move after the sudden death of her father. Although it has been a few months since her father's death, Lake is still experiencing residual sadness because of the loss of her happy family. Things are different now, and it is even more different when she finds herself in Michigan. She isn't happy to be there, but things begin to look up immediately when she meets the lovely man living next door to her. Will is a few years older than Lake, and they immediately hit it off. I mean they REALLY hit it off. I wouldn't go so far as to call it love at first sight, but they definitely find that there is a solid connection between each other. Within a few days they have gone on the best date ever in Lake's experience, and they are definitely way into each other.<br /><br />SPOILER AHEAD. READ ON AT YOUR OWN RISK.<br /><br />Then their happily ever after world tilts a bit on its axis. Lake shows up for her first day of school on the Monday following her amazing weekend of Will, only to see him in the hall at school as she starts searching for her third hour class. She goes to him, throws her arms around him, and he freaks out. Why? Well, young and lovely Will is actually a very young high school teacher at Lake's high school. He thought she was in college. She thought he was definitely not a teacher. And to add insult to injury . . . he's her third hour teacher. Noooooooo! Now that's trouble. Obviously they can't keep seeing each other. That's all kinds of wrong in almost any playbook in existence. High school teachers do not date their students. Even if the teacher is twenty-one and the student is eighteen. It just can't be done.<br /><br />So what to do now? They try to avoid each other. They try to be \\"just friends.\\" They occasionally get into snippy fits with each other. But they keep coming back to each other again and again. This becomes increasingly more frustrating as the novel continues. As a reader I am rooting for them to find a way to be together as a couple. No matter what Will may say, it is obvious that he wants to be with Lake. But even as my reading heart is wishing for this couple to make it work, my real life brain is saying that this wouldn't be a happy thing in a real life high school. Google any number of recent news stories on this sort of topic, and it becomes clear that situations like this do not generally have happy endings. And yet I continued to root for these two people who seem to be so meant for each other.<br /><br />In Slammed, Lake's mother gives her some great advise about finding a good man. She says:<br />\\"Does he treat you with respect at alltimes? That's the first question. The second question is, if he is the exact same person twenty years from now that he is today, would you still want to marry him? And finally, does he inspire you to want to be a better person? You find someone you can answer yes to all three, then you've found a good man.\\"<br /><br />That is why I can't stop rooting for this couple. Will is a good man. He inspires Lake to be a better person. He treats her with respect. A good man. Somehow this relationship has to succeed.<br /><br />Even with a crazy situation like this dominating her life, the difficulties are only beginning for Lake. She finds out that there is more to this move to Michigan than she originally believed, and this revelation is a doozy of a revelation. It will change Lake's life in a significant way, and it is in the midst of this struggle that I believe that Will truly shows his worth to her. Unfortunately it is mixed up in all the confusion of his being her teacher, so a lot of his awesome behavior is lost to her. But it was further proof of his goodness.<br /><br />I won't say more about the eventual ending or resolution of the various issues of the story. I will just say a few thoughts I had while I read. Most of all . . . I absolutely loved the character of Will. He was amazing in so many ways. The things he does for his younger brother and the consideration he gives to Lake's mother and to Lake as well were wonderful. He behaves in a way that seems very hurtful to Lake at one point in the novel (well, actually it is at several points), but once we discover his motivations for his actions, it makes him even more amazing in my opinion. The ending scene of the book was nice, but for me the most wonderful, incredible, amazing, swoon worthy, awwwwww moment of the book was when Will performed his Slam poetry, reading the \\"Lake\\" poem. My heart is still fluttering from that scene. I LOVED that poem and how he used words to so beautifully portray his love for Lake. I can't get them out of my head. That is writing genius in my mind. That is what makes a brilliant poem. Loved it!<br /><br />The poetry of the lyrics of the Avett Brothers played a good part in this novel. They aren't just words to read and then quickly move on to the main plot. They are words that have to simmer in your conscience, percolating until the meaning seeps into your heart, finding residence that resonates with you on a deeper level. I just really loved the inclusion of these lyrics in the novel. It is a richer novel for having them in it.<br /><br />Hoover does an amazing job of really portraying the struggle that Lake goes through as she realizes that she has fallen in love with Will. As a reader I could feel her desire warring with her head as she tried to find a way to make this situation work. I could feel her frustration. I could feel her moving through the stages of grief. The writing was very well done, keeping me turning pages until I could find a resolution that satisfied me.<br /><br />So am I satisfied? Yes! And no. I love the ending of this novel. It was what I wanted to find, even though it occurred in a way I didn't expect. But I was not satisfied to be done with Will and Lake's story. I wanted more. I want to re-enter the world of Slam poetry that displays the emotions of the writers in such a raw and real way. Hurray that there is a second novel in this series! I downloaded it right away so that I can continue their story. This was a wonderful discovery for me as a reader. Five stars!times? That's the first question. 0307949486|5.0|This is the first mystery novel I have read and thoroughly enjoyed it. I stayed up late each night reading it and enjoyed it so much that the day I finished it I went to the bookstore to buy the second book in the series. The characters were intriguing, the plot was interesting, the dialog flowed well and the writing was simple enough to knock out pages whenever you have a free moment. Though it's not a literary achievement (in the prose sense), the book affected me and is thought provoking insofar as its most difficult parts to read are based on crimes that happen frequently throughout the world and we, for the most part, choose to ignore them because they are at a minimum uncomfortable to accept.  As for the most difficult parts to read....<br /><br />If you don't do well with violence (specifically sexual abuse), then you'll likely have a difficult time with this book. Many will find it gratuitously violent and at first I felt the violence to be unnecessarily detailed; however, by the end of the book I felt it was necessary to illustrate the severity of the horrors. These crimes are perpetrated by absolute evil (both in this book and in real life). Without the detailed violence most readers won't feel the significance of these actions as we frequently mute uncomfortable thoughts in our minds to protect ourselves (unless, as in this book, we are forced to think about it/visualize it). However, in doing so I feel we do an injustice to the victims. Additionally, there's a risk the reader could sympathize with the antagonist(s) and I believe neither the antagonist(s) nor anyone like the antagonist(s) deserves an ounce of sympathy. As a result, I am in full support of this detailed violence as it has given me a new found understanding of what victims must deal with and how evil perpetrators of crimes like these truly are.<br /><br />The disturbing detail in which certain scenes of this book are written will cause many to not read it; however, it helps turns this book from simply a mystery into a haunting piece of work. It is because of this impact that I am giving it 5 stars.from simply a mystery into a haunting piece of work. It is because of this impact that I am giving it 5 stars.

B006Z7Z3R2|3.0|I find myself a bit torn in my opinion of The Innkeepers.  There's a lot to enjoy but there's also a fair amount to dislike about the film.  Director Ti West's story about an aging New England Inn in its final week of operation has a tone unlike most horror films.  There are a lot of elements that don't seem on the surface like they would mix together well, but the enjoyable cast makes the film eminently watchable.<br /><br />Claire (Paxton) and Luke (Healey) are a couple of twenty-something loafers who work at the Yankee Pedlar, a New England inn that is over a hundred years old.  With the owner on vacation, Claire and Luke are the only employees still working at the near-empty inn during its final week of operation.  With few guests to attend, and having to work 12 hour shifts the pair do what they can to amuse themselves and pass the time.  Fancying themselves amateur ghost hunters, they've setup a website to explore the legend of the Yankee Pedlar which is allegedly haunted by the spirit of a Madeline O'Malley, a woman who hung herself on her wedding day when her fianc&eacute; jilted her.<br /><br />As mentioned, The Innkeepers has a strange vibe to it.  The early part of the film has a good deal of comedy as the pair of Luke and Claire engage in various pursuits just to get through the day including drinking beer at the front counter, telling ghost stories to the young son of an annoying guest, just to get under her skin, and dealing with the wacky counterperson at the nearby coffee shop.  This, along with a slow pace doesn't fit with what you expect out of a horror film.  The tone changes abruptly with the arrival of Leanne Reese-Jones (McGillis) a former actress turned psychic.<br /><br />As Claire explores the inn at night with recording equipment, looking to pickup some EVP (electronic voice phenomena) she encounters voices whispering within the walls and the playing of a piano in the front lobby.  A terrified Claire runs to Leanne for help.  The psychic uses her ability to channel the spirits in the inn and warns Claire to stay clear of the basement.  The arrival of an elderly guest who wants to spend one last night in the honeymoon suite completes the transition from slacker comedy to full-on horror culminating with Claire's terrifying encounter with the inn's spirits.<br /><br />I suppose it depends on your outlook as to whether The Innkeeper's faults can be overlooked due to its positives or if it's positives are neutralized by the faults.  West's slow burn of a film develops the characters of Claire and Luke to the point where you can certainly relate to them.  The pair apparently have no prospects once the inn closes.  Claire's redoubtable spunkiness drives much of the action.  Last seen in the horrible film \\"Shark Night\\", Paxton appears here, sans tiny bikini and without make-up in a huge contrast from that film. There's a brilliantly funny scene as she is trying to open a dumpster lid with one hand and toss in a leaky plastic trash bag for the other...that is just a little too heavy for her to lift with a single hand and avoid whatever noxious contents are spilling out of the bag.  The dialog sparkles with a casual wit.  You feel like you're eavesdropping on a couple of real people when they are talking.<br /><br />But The Innkeepers has a major Achilles heel.  Too many questions are left unanswered at the film's conclusion; so many, in fact, that I found myself re-watching scenes to see if I missed the \\"Shamalayan\\" moment.  What did Leanne really see when she channeled the spirits?  And what was with her strange staring out of her room's window at the end?  For all of the development of the two leads, West is woefully short on any exposition when it comes to the spirits.  What are their motivations?  Why are they after Claire?  Why was it that Leanne's arrival seemed to have triggered the spirit's activity?  These issues prevent The Innkeepers from having the clean ending that most viewers desire.  But maybethat's what West was going for all along.<br /><br />Blu-Ray Extras<br /><br />Two Audio commentaries: One with Writer/director/editor Ti West, producers Peter Phok & Larry Fessenden, and second unit director/sound designer Graham Reznick; and the second with Ti West and stars Sara Paxton & Pat Healy.<br /><br />Behinds the Scenes Featurettewhat West was going for all along.<br /><br />Blu-Ray Extras<br /><br />Two Audio commentaries: One with Writer/director/editor Ti West, producers Peter Phok & Larry Fessenden, and second unit director/sound designer Graham Reznick; and the second with Ti West and stars Sara Paxton & Pat Healy.<br /><br />Behinds the Scenes Featurette

B0073U2F2Q|2.0|The Darkest Hour offers a new take on the alien invasion film with mixed results.  This American-Russian co-production finds two software developers Ben (Minghella) and Sean (Hirsch) traveling to Moscow where they hope to sell their new social networking app to a group of Russian investors.  However when they arrive at the meeting they find that their Swedish partner Skyler has stolen their idea and has already made a deal with the Russians.  Seeking to drown their sorrows they head to a nightclub where they meet a couple of women: Natalie, an American and her Australian friend Anne.<br /><br />The city suffers a total blackout and as the curious partiers head outside they see hundreds of wispy, glowing lights floating down from the sky.  Then lights turn out to he a hostile race of aliens who can disintegrate a person with a mere touch, leaving behind only a pile of ash.  The four, along with backstabbing business partner Skyler take refuge in a basement storeroom where they remain for a full day until its safe to venture out.  However they find the city almost completely devoid of any life with ashes strewn about.  Keeping an eye out for the near-invisible aliens, the group somehow must try to survive and make it out of Moscow.<br /><br />The aliens in The Darkest Hour are certainly original.  The glowing balls are mere shields protecting their bio-mechanical forms but this is about as far as the film goes with original ideas.  In the end it falls back on plot contrivances that have been used in every alien invasion film from War of the Worlds to Independence Day, often blatantly ripping off both of those films.  There's even the Deus Ex Machina moment when they figure out how to kill the aliens. The film is muddled with confusing and contrasting uses of the aliens powers.  Ben and Sean turn out to be typical film characters who are much smarter than anyone should be about an alien life form they've never encountered. After hiding behind a glass display in a clothing store, they determine that the aliens \\"see\\" using a kind of radar that detects a human's electro magnetic signature.  I mean, that exactly what I would have thought, too.<br /><br />Yet it begs the question that if glass somehow blocks this ability then why aren't the people who were in their cars safe at the time of the attack.  As they explore the city they encounter an electrician who has covered the floors and walls of his apartment in metal grates which can somehow keep the aliens out.  Later however, we learn that they are mining our planets metals which they feed on.  So is metal good or bad for the aliens?  I still have no idea.<br /><br />The film is essentially the same scene played over and over...move to a new place, explore it, encounter aliens, and run.  At no point does Director Chris Gorak stop long enough to offer anything remotely resembling character development.  I mean what was the point to having the Swedish partner steal their idea only to turn around and have them all act like nothing happened.  Sure, an alien invasion might tend to make you forget the rest of your problems but why toss that sub-plot in there anyway?<br /><br />I mean it gets to the point when you actually start rooting for the aliens.  At least a little energy is infused in the last third of the film when they meet a gung-ho group of Russian soldiers who've found a way to hurt the aliens.  By this time though the film seems far longer than its 90 minute runtime. B000002L7R|4.0|If you're Prince, you do so in the most unpredictable of ways. Almost nothing on this album sounds as if it could have fit in comfortably on its predecessor. This was an incredibly bold move. Beginning with the '80s, it was almost unheard of for a pop artist to follow up a blockbuster album only a mere ten months later. Look at 1984's other major hit albums. Madonna took nearly two years to follow up 1984's \\"Like a Virgin.\\" Springsteen waited three years to release a new studio album after \\"Born in the USA.\\" Two years for Van Halen to follow up \\"1984.\\"<br /><br />Why is that significant? To put it into context, \\"Purple Rain\\" spent 24 consecutive weeks at number one on Billboard's album chart. It was only three months after \\"Purple Rain\\" relinquished it's stranglehold on the top spot that \\"Around the World\\" was released. The then-new album was seen by many as a disappointment commercially because it \\"only\\" spent three weeks at number one, and \\"only\\" sold three million or so copies.<br /><br />Not that any of that really matters more than a quarter of a century later. The most casual fans only know \\"Raspberry Beret\\" and \\"Pop Life,\\" but there's much more to this album. \\"Tamborine\\" is one of the most insanely funky creations he ever released. \\"America\\" - a near miss on the Top 40 singles chart - was a surprisingly right-leaning political anthem (maybe not so surprising, actually, considering earlier tunes like \\"Ronnie Talk to Russia\\" and \\"Free\\"). \\"Paisley Park,\\" lest anyone think Prince was a hardliner, asks \\"Whoever said that elephants were stronger than mules?\\" Despite a too-long, meandering intro, \\"Condition of the Heart\\" is a lovely ballad with idiosyncratic lyrics (\\"There was a woman from the ghetto/Who made funny faces/Just like Clara Bow\\").<br /><br />The only real mistep comes in the form of \\"The Ladder,\\" a quasi-spritual snoozer. \\"Temptation\\" is better, though it is far from classic Prince. The guitar playing is hot, Eddie M's sax introduces live horns into Prince's recorded work, and the confrontation with God is, well, kind of silly. Together these tracks comprise roughly one-third of the album's running time. The seven songs that came before them are all superior, so the album lands with thud rather than exploding with a climax (pretty much defined by \\"Purple Rain\\"). The last section of the album understandably leaves the listener with mixed feelings. But start it over again and soak up the greatness of the first two-thirds and you might come to agree with the notion that this is an underrated album.

B000002L9B|5.0|I'm not sure that there is a more moving song in the Prince catalog than \\"Sometimes It Snows In April.\\" The lyrics and melody, not to mention the skeletal arrangement, all combine to make one of the man's overlooked masterpieces.<br /><br />This is an adventurous, daring, and complex album that has somehow faded from the landscape of great pop albums. Well, that's actually partly because it has never been remastered and reissued. Prince is one of the very few major artists who has yet to see even ONE of his albums reissued. He was still breathing rarefied air at the time of this album. Compared to recent albums like \\"20ten,\\" \\"MPLSound,\\" \\"Planet Earth,\\" or \\"3121,\\" this sounds like the work of an entirely different artist.<br /><br />\\"Kiss\\" is the most popular moments, credit for its arrangement goes to Mazarati, who re-worked Prince's acoustic demo into the work of funk genius we hear on the album. \\"Mountains\\" was a hit too, though only Prince fans know that - casual fans don't have that one on the compilations. \\"Anotherloverholenyohead\\" was a failed single, which only proves that commercial success means nothing - this is one brilliantly executed song. \\"Girls & Boys\\" is another funk workout that perfectly capture's its author's horny narcissism with the simple line, \\"She had the cutest ass he'd ever seen/She did 2, they were meant 2 be.\\"<br /><br />Prince recorded the album's opening quartet of songs sequentially, sitting at his drum set and laying down the rhythm. All four songs in a row. Told the engineer to start rolling, and he launched into it, with the lyrics taped to the wall. He then built the tracks up from that point. This is according to Per Nilson in his meticulously researched and indispensible book \\"DMSR.\\" Anyway, that's artistic VISION.<br /><br />\\"Life Can Be So Nice\\" might be the most polarizing track on the album. But it's an amazingly dense, multi-layered production with some great, idiosyncratic lyrics, i.e. \\"No one plays the clarinet/The way youplay my heart.\\" The man doesn't write like that anymore.<br /><br />The very recently departed (01/26/2012) Clare Fischer arranged the string parts for these songs. They are breathtaking, lending a very distinct sound that expands on the richness of Prince's songs. Fischer did similarly great work on many other Prince recordings.<br /><br />\\"Parade\\" has been criticized for being tied in some ways to the characters in the film \\"Under the Cherry Moon.\\" Nonsense. The French overtones on songs like \\"Do U Lie?\\" and \\"Girls & Boys\\" only adds to the timelessness of the album. Yes, the character of Christopher Tracy is name-checked in the opening and closing tracks. So what? Does anyone complain that the Beatles sang about the fictional people Sgt. Pepper and Billy Shears? Even if the movie had not existed, the name Christopher Tracy doesn't render the songs incomprehensible or invalid in any way.<br /><br />The only way to improve this album would be to remastered it and add the following bonus tracks: \\"Alexa de Paris,\\" \\"Love or Money,\\" and the incredible extended mixes of \\"Kiss,\\" \\"Anotherlover,\\" and \\"Mountains.\\" Maybe someday. Until then, the album can be acquired inexpensively. If you haven't heard it and have read this far, you need it.

0670022950|3.0|This work, on which the author obviously spent a tremendous amount of energy and work, was for me a great disappointment.  Where I had hoped for a scholarly treatment, I found instead a polemic in which, as other readers have observed, whatever doesn't fit the thesis is ignored or underplayed.  For example, in his first chapter, which attempts to show us that ancient society was an unremitting bloodbath (one wonders how, in the midst of such violence, ancient societies achieved what they did--how could the Egyptians have built the pyramids if they were killing each other off at the rates Pinker projects), Pinker describes the Ten Commandments as the Jews' \\"great moral code that outlaws engraved images and coveting of livestock, but gives a pass to slavery, rape, torture, mutilation, and genocide of neighboring tribes.\\" (p. 7) This is so one-sided as to be shocking: no mention of the fact that the Ten Commandments outlawed murder, stealing, and adultery, required honoring one's parents, and prohibited bearing false witness--all provisions that, it would seem, were aimed at reducing violence.  But, since that doesn't fit Pinker's thesis, these aspects of the ancient biblical moral code are ignored.  Another weird problem: Pinker uses the Homeric epics and the Bible as reliable evidence of how life was lived in ancient societies, without ever questioning the assumption that they are accurate portrayals. Would one rely on \\"Lonesome Dove\\" for an accurate portrayal of life in the Old West?  No, one would seek out historical works on the period.  It is very interesting in this regard that Pinker uses Homer's poems rather than the ancient histories of, say, Alexander's conquests or Caesar's Gallic Wars.  As others have noted, Pinker asserts the unremitting violence of primitive man, without mentioning that this interpretation is very controversial and not at all generally accepted.  To turn to a more modern period, in arguing that the violence of World War II pales in comparison to past massacres--Pinker's point (itself controversial and not intuitively obvious to this reader) is that, since the population of the world was much less in the past, World War II is not as bad proportionately--he uses estimates of earlier casualties that are highly contested, but gives no real explanation that this is so.  For example, he puts the death toll from the An Lushan Revolt at 35 million, without making clear how debated that number is and why, in fact, there are those who say the death toll was far less.  As I read the book, I felt more and more let down by the lack of objectivity that I found.  And, in the end, what is the use of such a work, since the evidence relied upon is basically massaged to support the author's thesis?  I sincerely hope that what we have here is not a more modern version of Normal Angell's 1910 classic \\"The Great Illusion,\\" which argued that due to the integration of modern economies, war and militarism were becoming obsolete.  As we know, four years later World War I broke out.  (Prof. Pinker might say, of course, that Angell was correct, if for the wrong reasons, and that WWI and WWII were the last gasps of an older world.  Let's hope so.)  On a positive note: I must add to the above criticisms this note: when Professor Pinker was writing about what he knows best--human psychology and the way the human mind works--I found what he wrote helpful and genuinely worthwhile (which explains the three stars).rison to past massacres--Pinker's point (itself controversial and not intuitively obvious to this reader) is that, since the population of the world was much less in the past, World War II is not as bad proportionately--he uses estimates of earlier casualties that are highly contested, but gives no real explanation that this is so.  For example, he puts the death toll from the An Lushan Revolt at 35 million, without making clear how debated that number is and why, in fact, there are those who say the death toll was far less.  As I read the book, I felt more and more let down by the lack of objectivity that I found.  And, in the end, what is the use of such a work, since the evidence relied upon is basically massaged to support the author's thesis? B002IFT1ZA|4.0|this is a truly magnificent work in the making. sporting a massive cast of top-notch actors (including Sean Bean, who played Boromir in Lord of the Rings), Game of Thrones is a sprawling story of civil unrest in the fantasy kingdom of Westeros, where summer and winter can last for decades.<br /><br />this is NOT, however, a Lord of the Rings-style fantasy thingit. it's more comparable to The Tudors in Middle-Earth; fantasy elements are very subtle, often only half-seen or hinted at. the real story lies in the power struggles two of Westeros's most prominent noble families, the Starks and the Lannisters. it's a very political story, with lots of plotting, veiled threats, and double entendres. all of the characters are well-realized, deep, and magnificently portrayed by their actors. the story gets off to a slow start, but ultimately it becomes absolutely riveting.<br /><br />visually, the show is almost like a movie. we get lots of gorgeous shots of castles, from the squat, grim, ugly towers of Winterfell to the soaring spires of King's Landing, or the cold, forbidding ice cliffs of the 800-foot-high Wall of the North. landscapes are rendered beautifully, with not a single hitch in the CGI, although at times the backdrops look a bit like painted murals (i think this is an intentional stylistic choice).<br /><br />the only criticisms i have are these: first, the show does stumble a bit through the first few episodes. i can hardly blame the producers, though. the book sports a huge and intricate web of characters, all of whom have histories that need to be explained. so naturally, the exposition sometimes trips over itself in trying to fit an 800+ page novel into a ten-episode season. the story really takes off after episode 6, and from that point on it's smooth sailing.<br /><br />my second complaint is a small thing. the fight scenes are well-choreographed and practiced, but they don't quite seem real. the actors know the choreography, they just haven't been taught how to move like swordsmen. this is just a personal pet peeve.<br /><br />all in all, Game of Thrones is a definite Must See. it is deep, dangerous, and mature. the characters are very realistic and likable, especially the dwarf Tyrion, whose cutting, mocking sense of humor always shows up at just the right moment to draw a laugh from what would otherwise be an overwhelmingly dark and cynical series.

B00004XOWM|5.0|Limp Bizkit's \\"The Chocolate Starfish and the Hot Dog Flavoured Water\\" is without a doubt one of the most important musical works of the previous millennium and a fitting exclamation point to mark the end of the second Renaissance known as the Twentieth Century.<br /><br />I remember when I was first introduced to this veritable powder keg of creative energy in the Autumn of 1999.<br /><br />It was a simpler time.  Sega Dreamcasts were selling like hotcakes.  WCW Monday Nitro brought the thrill of live wrestling competitions, once afforded only to those with the means to witness these dazzling events in person, into the homes of ordinary Americans.  Lance Armstrong had won his first Tour de France, and Woodstock '99 delivered the message of peace and free love to a new generation of idealistic, starry-eyed youths.<br /><br />Enter \\"Nookie,\\" from Limp Bizkit's groundbreaking sophomore effort, \\"Significant Other.\\"<br /><br />I first heard the now iconic strains of this masterpiece while driving to Shakey's Pizza for a post-cram session luncheon with my dear friend and schoolmate Alistair Brestmane.  I stifled a gasp when its chorus swelled to a glorious crescendo:<br /><br />\\"I did it all for the nookie (Come on) / The nookie (Come on) / So you can take that cookie / And stick it up your (YEAH!) / And stick it up your (YEAH!) / And stick it up your (YEAH!) / And stick it up your...\\"<br /><br />I had no choice but to pull over then and there.  Alistair didn't question why.  I think he knew that, together in that car, we had experienced nothing short of a watershed moment.  We sat there for the following three minutes, neither of us daring to utter a word, as Fred Durst, Wes Borland, Sam Rivers, John Otto, Mike Smith and DJ Lethal stuck a defiant fork in the roast goose that was the Twentieth Century.<br /><br />You see, 1999 was not all mirth and gaiety.  As the sun began to rise on the new millennium, the looming spectre of the Y2K computer glitch cast its ominous shadow over the world.  Like frightened goats, people everywhere stormed their local haberdasheries to stock up on sundries like water, electricity generators, dehydrated meals and Code Red Mountain Dew, for fear of what the impending End might visit upon us.  Around the world, streets emptied out as families huddled together in their basements to read from the Book of Revelation and the eleventh chapter of the Bhagavad Gita and beseech God for mercy.<br /><br />But like the first seagull spotted from a tempest-tossed barge, Limp Bizkit arrived just as it seemed that all was lost and declared to the world, using not seagull screams but their innovative nu-metal sound, \\"Land ho!\\"<br /><br />Or so Alistair put it when the song was over and I turned off the radio.<br /><br />Like Bob Dylan before them, Limp Bizkit used music to soothe a society gone mad as it faced its own self-destruction.  I like to think that Fred Durst knew this, and modeled his oeuvre after Dylan's; for every \\"Blowing in the Wind,\\" a \\"Stink Finger.\\"  And for every \\"Blonde on Blonde,\\" a \\"Three Dollar Bill, Yall$.\\"<br /><br />And like the Beatles, these six lads from Jacksonville, Florida made us all rethink what music could be.  Which is why I compare \\"Chocolate Starfish and the Hot Dog Flavored Water\\" to the Beatles' masterwork, \\"Abbey Road.\\"<br /><br />Who doesn't hear echoes of \\"Octopus's Garden\\" in lyrics like this?:<br /><br />\\"Ain't life a bitch? / A f...ed up bitch / A f...ed up sore with a f...ed up stitch / A f...ed up head / Is a f...ed up shame / Swinging on my nuts / Is a f...ed up game... Hooo Haaa Haaaw! Listen up baby / You can't bring me down / I don't think so / I don't want some / You better check yourself / Before you wreck yourself / Kiss my star fish / My chocolate Starfish, punk / Kiss my star fish / My chocolate Starfish, punk.\\"<br /><br />Alistair was sent away to military school the following Spring.  I never saw my dear friend again, but on rainy nights I like to fire up my gramophone, make myself a cup of Earl Gray, and lounge on the chaise with my Pomeranians (Mitsy and Oppenheimer) as I lose myself in some Limp Bizkit and think back on those days, those beautiful days with Alistair.  The time we skipped school and had a picnic in a canoe.  The time our team won the Fourth Division Young Men's Polo Tourney.  The time we were showering in the locker room after the Fourth Division Young Men's Polo Tourney and I slipped and fell and a part of Alistair's body accidentally went in my mouth.<br /><br />Those bright and beautiful days are forever etched in my memory.<br /><br />And if by some chance happening, or twist of fate, or by heavenly design, you stumble across this review, Alistair, know that you are missed.  You are loved.  And there is plenty of room on this chaise longue for two.

0894803123|4.0|We are ice cream fanatics - our family consumes about a quart per week.  And we have been making virtually all of our own ice cream for the past 15 years,with a Cuisinart. That's over 750 1-quart batches of home made ice cream, and at least half of those batches were made using recipes from this book.  The basic recipe is uncooked, and consists of cream, milk, eggs, and sugar.  Custard based ice creams have their place, as do those eggless versions made by heating milk/cream with a cornstarch/milk paste (see below), but they are more time consuming and dirty a lot of dishes.  So I keep coming back to Ben and Jerry's easy to make, raw egg recipes.  The reason is simple: nothing beats the pure, fresh flavor of an uncooked ice cream with few ingredients: no corn starch, no corn syrup, no cream cheese.<br /><br />So what are the problems with these recipes, and what can be done about them:<br /><br />1. Salmonella in raw eggs.  If you buy the typical, inexpensive supermarket eggs from filthy, crowded factory farms, then you should worry about the risk of salmonella in raw eggs.  Worry less if you buy \\"cage free\\" eggs from the supermarket.  Worry still less if you buy eggs laid by chickens on pasture, as you might find from a local farm.  We don't worry at all because we get our eggs from our own backyard chickens who roam outside in a spacious paradise and sleep in a squeaky clean chicken coop.  And the eggs are never more than 2 days old when we use them for ice cream.  You can buy pasteurized (therefore no salmonella) factory farm eggs at the grocery store, but I personally never do this because I don't want to support any kind of factory farm.<br /><br />2. While the texture of the ice cream made using the recipes in this book is excellent for the first few days, it does become icy rather quickly.  So if it's going to sit in the freezer for more than 3-4 days, a cooked ice cream (either custard or eggless) will maintain its smooth, creamy mouth-feel for longer.  I use a cooked recipe if I am making a flavor that only 1 or 2 of us like, because it will not be eaten so quickly.<br /><br />3. The chocolate ice cream recipes in this book do not work well for me.  Jerry's chocolate is too gritty, and Ben's chocolate doesn't blend right -- the chocolate seizes.  Maybe they work sometimes for some people, but after 2 flops with each recipe, I gave up.  So for chocolate ice creams, I use either a custard based recipe (my favorite for chocolate), or the Milkiest Chocolate Ice Cream in the World (from the book Jeni's Splendid Ice Creams).  For a fool-proof, quick and dirty version of chocolate ice cream, reduce the sugar in Ben and Jerry's sweet cream base, and stir in Hershey's chocolate syrup to taste, before pouring the liquid into the ice cream machine.  Yeah, the flavor is far inferior to ice cream made with melted, unsweetened chocolate, but hey, if you're in a rush, and it's just going to be eaten by kids who won't care, this is the way to go.<br /><br />For vanilla or sweet cream based ice creams (oreo, cookie dough, chocolate chip, etc.) NOTHING beats the pure, fresh, raw flavor of Ben and Jerry's recipes.  During berry and peach seasons, we consume a quart of vanilla ice cream within 2 days, so never bother with cooked recipes.  In winter, when chickens are resting and we are short on eggs, Jeni's eggless technique of cooking the ingredients with a milk/cornstarch slurry and adding both cream cheese and corn syrup for smoother texture, is pretty decent for flavor (if you don't mind a hint of cream cheese in all your ice cream flavors), and stays smooth for a long time in the freezer.<br /><br />Another alternative, if you don't have, or don't want to use, eggs: Omit the eggs from Ben and Jerry's recipes - just reduce the amount of sugar slightly, or increase the amount of milk or cream, so you won't have too much sugar relative to the volume of liquid ingredients.  But an uncooked eggless ice cream gets icy even more quickly, so don't use it for ice cream that will sit in the freezer for more than 2 days.<br /><br />Some people might find this ice cream to be \\"cloying\\" due to the high fat content (recipes use twice as much cream as milk).  We don't, but if you do, you can reduce the cream and increase the milk.  The problem is that reducing the fat content will make the ice cream less smooth. You really need a high fat content for a raw ice cream to be super smooth.  Jeni's technique of cooking the ingredients and using corn starch, corn syrup, and cream cheese makes the lowest fat, super smooth ice cream I know of, but the flavor just isn't is good, IMO.<br /><br />Oh, I should say that if you add fruit to an uncooked ice cream, the increased water content will make it icier, so we don't mix the fruit in unless it will be eaten within a day or two: we usually just top vanilla ice cream with the fruit.  If you must have strawberry or mango or peach ice cream, a cooked recipe will yield a product that stays smooth for a long time.  Ben and Jerry's uncooked peanut butter ice cream, on the other hand, is fabulous, since the fat content of the peanut butter adds to the smooth/creamy texture.  No need to waste time on a cooked peanut butter ice cream.  Same for egg nog ice cream: the uncooked Ben and Jerry's recipe is outstanding.<br /><br />I cannot comment on the cookie dough and brownie recipes in this book, because I use my own recipes for those, and just add them to Ben and Jerry's sweet cream base.  We don't like sorbet, so I can't comment on those recipes either.<br /><br />Hope this helps!

If I am reading Amazon's return policy correctly, I could lose up to half the value since the box has been opened and the device used. I pushed for an RMA and they gave me one. So I pack up the watch and send it in. This is when I find out that their RMA status on their website can take up to \\"10-12 business days\\" to update, so it's not useful. Finally today my RMA status has updated. \\"Your product has been backordered. Please contact Product Support for an expected shipment date.\\" Production shortfalls happen and I understand that...assuming I had been contacted directly instead of finding out when they finally got around to updating their website.<br /><br />I realize that 99% of the time, Garmin makes a great product and it works right out of the box but had I known that I'd be three weeks into this watch and still not have a working one, I would have looked harder at the Timex and Motorola products.

Finally, my dad brought it home to me a couple weeks after its release and I almost had a stroke because I was so frackin excited. At least the wait was worth it. So so so so so so so so worth it. Lauren Oliver brings back everything we adored in Delirium--beautiful prose, a haunting society, high emotion, relentless tension--and even more: edgier writing, sharper beliefs and goals, and a much tougher lifestyle. Lauren Oliver has created yet another book that will rage in my soul for my entire life.    I don't even know how to coherently express my love for this book, besides, \\"OMGOMGO MGKDGNIQUERBGIBDNKASFJN FGIHJBFGVAN AHHH YAYAYAYAYAYAYAAYAYAYAYYAYAYAYAYA OMG.  PWENFHOIABXCKJFD!\\" I feel like Lauren Oliver took a stroll through my heart and discovered exactly what will make me love and break my heart and BLOW MY FRACKIN MIND. Because that's what she does. Every word builds me up to break me down to build me back up. I'm not sure how she manages to fit all these feelings in one book, but she does.    This book has a lot more action than the first. Whereas Delirium was about Lena discovering what she wants and figuring out how to grab hold of it, Pandemonium was about Lena fighting for what she wants and struggling to hold on to it. The book alternates between \\"Then\\" and \\"Now.\\"    In the 'Then' section, Lena has just arrived at the Wilds and she is struggling to recuperate--physically and emotionally. And yet, she doesn't back down. She wants to get her strength back and she wants to carry on. She turns her weaknesses into strengths. We're introduced to new characters, which I absolutely fell for. They all have an air of mystery surrounding them because nobody in the Wilds is particularly fond of discussing the past. But their strength and kindness is evident even if their lifestyle is harsh and their words are terse. There's a lot of despair and hopelessness in this section.    In the 'Now' section, Lena has created a tough outer shell around herself. She tries not to think of the past and just keep doing what she knows is right. I think I liked this section a lot better than 'Then.' This section is just a little more fierce and contains a lot more action. I also feel more connected to Lena in this section.    I just couldn't bring myself to fall for the new guy. I mean, not even just because I adore Alex and I miss the hell out of him in this book. But also because the new guy is so naive that I just get this little boy vibe from him. I just couldn't. I mean, he's a good character but he's not good for Lena, in my opinion. I also missed Hana and Grace. I haven't read the Hana novella, so I'm not sure what happens to her, but I do hope she will be in the next book.    The ending, of course, was epic. While I kind of expected it, when it happened I was completely taken aback. I expected nothing less from Lauren Oliver. She rips me apart and stitches me back together over and over and over in the best possible way. I cannot wait for the next book. This is a series I am one hundred percent invested in and will never forget. It makes me feel so much more than I can possibly describe.

B002ZCY7PU|4.0|Charles 'Chuck' Bartowski and his handlers, Sarah Walker and John Casey, have successfully defeated FULCRUM, a rogue intelligence agency. The Intersect, the combined intelligence database of the entire United States which has been downloaded into Chuck's brain, has been radically upgraded. Now Chuck has access to advanced weapons and kung fu skills, amongst other abilities. But Chuck's emotions are getting in the way of him being able to do his job. A new agent, Daniel Shaw, is assigned to the team to help train Chuck as a spy, but this has unexpected results.<br /><br />After the relentlessly entertaining second season of Chuck, the third season gets off to a surprisingly weak start. Rather than picking up immediately on Season 2's cliffhanger ending (where Chuck comes into possession of the Intersect 2.0), we rejoin the action six months later. This causes problems even with Chuck's elastic notions of plausibility (why are Sarah and Casey hanging around Burbank for six months when Chuck isn't there?) and necessitates a lot of backtracking and flashbacks to fill in the gap. Once we're past the hurdle of the first few episodes (and a somewhat dubious Vinnie Jones guest role), however, things improve a lot. The second season's format of stringing together several multi-episode arcs into one cohesive whole is repeated and is almost as successful as previously. Brandon Routh is decent in the new role of Shaw, with the writers not wasting any opportunity to highlight his previous major role as Superman (even draping him in the American flag in one amusing scene).<br /><br />As usual, the season has a good mix of comedy and drama, with some great stand-alone stories (Armand Assante's turn as a somewhat demented, American-friendly version of Castro is especially entertaining) standing alongside the ongoing story arcs. Most satisfying is the unexpected way the show's set-up suddenly changes. Major characters discover Chuck's secret with little forewarning, altering the show's premise for the better by dropping the 'secret identity' storyline just as it was starting to get a little stale. Chuck and Sarah's relationship is moved onto another level, again just as the 'will they/won't they' angle was running out of steam. Even Casey is given a stronger personal storyline, as he discovers a family he never knew he had and becomes conflicted over contacting them or not. And, as usual, the more serious spy stuff is balanced out nicely by the lunacy going on over at the Buy More store.<br /><br />Overall, the third season of Chuck (****) is funny, self-aware and entertaining. It's not quite as a good as the second season, due to a dodgy set-up in the first few episodes that results in a lot of backtracking and wheel-spinning and the fact that the new bad guys, the Ring, are identical to FULCRUM. Beyond that, the show evolves its premise and characters in compelling new directions and shows a willingness to change even fundamental parts of the premise when necessary. The season is available now in the UK (DVD) and USA (DVD, Blu-Ray).

I thought it was a very effective means to convey the shifting and unsteady world in which the characters of the novel live.  Why shouldn't we as readers be unsettled and disoriented as we read this novel - the topic and story are incredibly disturbing and tragic.  I think our discomfort is exactly what the author intended.  As has been mentioned in other reviews, if you stick with it to the end and embrace the authors style, you'll find the ending very satisfying.

B005FI6IRG|5.0|Many in the music world have eagerly awaited the release of this album, which features two of the most gifted male sopranos: Philippe Jaroussky and Max Emmanuel Cencic. Those listeners who have marveled at Jaroussky's exploration of Vivaldi's operas through his \\"Vivaldi Heroes\\" Album, and at Cenci's disc of Handel arias, would certainly embrace an album of duets featuring both artists together. Adding the direction and collaboration of the veteran conductor William Christie simply sweetens the anticipation! However, listeners expecting more music like jaw-dropping Vivaldi arias and exciting Handel melodies will not be getting what they anticipate. Instead, the artists have chosen the more intimate, gentle and introspective chamber music of the early Baroque: composers such as Bononcini, Mancini, and Alessandro Scarlatti. These works were originally composed for the most gifted singers of the day, and were meant for small audiences of musical intellectuals. The instrumental accompaniment is minimal: a pair of violins perhaps, a cello, harpsichord,  theorbo or lute. The choices of music include chamber duets (single duets set to poetry), cantatas for two soprano voices, and solo cantatas. In fact, two of the works recorded here (a cantata by Mancini and a cantata by the great operatic master Porpora) are solo cantatas, and feature Jaroussky or Cencic singing alone. There are a total of eight works featured, and the recording engineers graciously separate the recitatives from the arias and duets so that your favorites can be repeated with ease. The music is quiet, beautifully luscious, and sung with sensitivity and love by both singers. Their voices fit together perfectly, flowing through the music with ease and great sensitivity to text and meaning (as noted by William Christie in the liner notes, and one gets the idea that this disc was his brain child). The best way to enjoy this album is to listen with intent in a darkened room, alone or with an intimate friend, aglass of fine wine, and simply let the gorgeous sounds wash over you. It is a true delight to know that this beautiful music has been resurrected.

B004VF68AQ|4.0|I've been a JA fan since the early 90s... I've been through the ups, the downs, the breakups, the reunions, everything. I remember listening, mesmerized, to Classic Girl on a distant, fuzzy FM station as a kid in the early 90s. Those were the days, indeed. All that said, I think The Great Escape Artist is a very good album from the band that defined alternative rock and provided the platform to launch the grunge movement.<br /><br />Is The Great Escape Artist as genre-defining or influential as their self-titled 1987 debut record or Nothing's Shocking? No. Is the music up to the par set by these albums, Ritual, and Kettle Whistle? Yes. Even the best songs on Strays, an album which I found to be surprisingly middling, can't touch the best songs on Artist. Where Strays sort of flowed along at an even keel, never approaching the heights of greatness (or the depths of mindless pop rock), Artist ebbs and flows all over the spectrum.<br /><br />There's nothing I despise more (well, there is, but my point wouldn't hit as hard if I worded it as such) than a band that doesn't evolve, grow, or (god forbid) mature. Take a band like Faith No More and compare them to a band like AC/DC (sorry, love you guys!) and you'll see what I mean. While the former can churn out an album that'll have you checking the label to make sure you're listening to right group, the latter can (albeit successfully) remake the same album over and over and be content.<br /><br />The Great Escape Artist sounds like the ideal evolution of a band that started out as straight alt rock before they delved into electronic music and finally found a happy medium between the two. I would not be a satisfied listener if Jane's Addiction attempted to remake Nothing's Shocking over and over again. Thankfully, they have not. On the flipside, it's unrealistic to expect a band like Jane's Addiction to repeatedly revolutionize rock over and over again. How many bands can you name that defined an entire genre with EVERY release? While I can think of many great bands, I can't think of any that fit this criteria. People whining about Artist not being as influential or groundbreaking as Nothing's Shocking can therefor go away, for all I care. (Likewise people crying about Eric Avery. He was here, now he's not. Deal with it.)<br /><br />Let's take a look at the music itself, because at the end of the day, that's all that really matters. There's nothing I like more (well, there is, but...) than albums that grow on you over time. I'll admit it-- I wasn't overly impressed with The Great Escape Artist on my first (or even second) listen. Often times, these sorts of albums are precisely the ones that become favorites down the road. In the case of Artist, there is SO MUCH going on sonically in every song that it's simply impossible to take it all in with just one or two listens. Before you know it, you're picking up on subtle nuances in the music and lyrics, actually anticipating your next listen. Songs like Underground and End to the Lies are razor-sharp and hit hard. Not since the one-two punch of Up the Beach/Ocean Size has a JA album opened so well. I'm especially a fan of lyrics on Artist. I've read a lot of comments here panning the lyrics; they're boring, uninspired... Are we listening to the same album? The lyrics on End to the Lies, for example, are far edgier and insightful than anything on Strays. Yeah, Perry no longer sings about jacking razors or pissing on himself in the shower, but then again he's no longer a kid.<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, this album is all over the place and much less consistent than Strays or some of the earlier records. In some ways, this is actually a strength. There are moments that really \\"wow\\" you. There are others (not many... ok, maybe one) that have you reaching for the \\"Next\\" button. It's the lulls, however, that make the peaks hit you even harder. The album opens with two power hitters, then sort of drops off for a couple tracks before coming back strong with I'll Hit You Back, one of the album's best. Splash a Little Water on It was initially one of my favorite tracks, after repeated listens, it's near the bottom of my list. Funny how that works out sometimes. Broken People is a beautiful song and fights a good fight for best track alongside End to the Lies. Broken People is Artist's answer to the mellow Jane Says on Nothing's Shocking or Ritual's Classic Girl. I still haven't decided how I feel about album-closer Words Right Out of My Mouth. I like the fast-paced rocker vibe, but I don't know if I like the song structure. Time will tell. Curiosity Kills and Ultimate Reason are certainly more than competent efforts and manage to assert themselves quite successfully with catchy hooks. Ironically, my least favorite track on the record would have to be the \\"epic single\\" Irresistible Force. To me, this song just isn't JA. I can't dig it. This was the first track I heard from the album, before it was even released, and as a result my expectations were pretty low going in.<br /><br />It's no coincidence I've chosen Strays as a point of comparison throughout this piece. Strays is as close a contemporary as you'll get to Artist and features the same lineup (Farrell, Navarro, Perkins, Chaney), even if guest keyboardist-guitarist-bassist-jack-of-all-trades Dave Sitek didn't show up until the Artist sessions. If Strays has any leg up on Artist, it's the mix. I've seen criticisms of this in comments here, and I'd have to agree. The mix is somewhat muddy, and the guitars way too low. Guitars should be front and center on a JA album, and don't even get me started on the whole Loudness War B.S.  I sincerely hope whomever produced and mixed this album is fired for their next outing. Strays, by comparison, sounds very crisp and clear with plenty of loud, rockin' guitars.<br /><br />It's a shame so many people haven't given Artist enough of a chance to really appreciate it. It's much more evolved than Strays and I personally can't wait to see where they go next. Although, I'm not sure why they need Dave Sitek. If they're going to bring in someone to \\"help out,\\" I'd much rather see an appearance by, say, Peter DiStefano. Maybe next time.
B007SYWFRM|5.0|a w e s o m e g a m e l o v e I t!! f o r real
1434404374|4.0|Agatha Christie wrote this book -- supposedly after a dare by a relative -- in 1916, although it wasn't published until 1920.  It was her first novel and introduced Hercule Poirot, the retired Belgian detective who was to star in many of her later novels and short stories.  All of the hallmarks of Christie's later books are evident here:  In addition to Poirot, we have narration by Arthur Hastings -- at this point only a lieutenant rather than a captain, as he later was -- who right from the start is oblivious to his own obtuseness and skeptical of Poirot's deductive abilities, a murder at a stately country home, key evidence necessary to solve the mystery given during the narration, and some very red herrings.  As a first effort, it is a bravura performance and it is no wonder that it was enough to launch Christie on a decade's long career.<br /><br />If this novel has any significant drawbacks, it is that some of Poirot's deductions are so convoluted as to be a bit implausible and some of the herrings are a little too red.  I also recently read \\"Curtain,\\" which Christie wrote in the mid-1940s, although she held back publication until the 1970s because it was written to be Poirot's last case.  I would say \\"The Mysterious Affair at Styles\\" is in most respects a better book, even though \\"Curtain\\" was written near the end of Christie's prime.  Certainly, \\"Styles\\" is a more enjoyable book because the gloom of Poirot's decline hangs over \\"Curtain.\\"<br /><br />I believe the copyright on this book has lapsed and it is now in the public domain.  Hence, the proliferation of editions currently available.  Curiously, the new series of paperbacks by Harper, which include just about every book Christie has written, do not include \\"Styles.\\"  That is too bad because the Harper paperbacks are first rate.  One word of warning:  The free e-book versions apparently do not include several figures that are included in the print editions.  The edition that I read includes these figures,although the printing of them is a bit blurry for some reason.  So, if you are a Christie fan, it may be worth your while to spend a few buck to buy a print edition.

B004EPYZV2|3.0|I enjoyed MI-GP for the first hour and a half.  Then I became impatient for it to end.  The action sequences are spectacular - well, as long as you don't think about them.  An essential aspect of an action film is a believable sense of danger.  The problem with making characters impervious to injury is the sense of danger evaporates.  It doesn't matter how scary what they're doing is if you know they will just get up and walk away at the end of the scene.  The many ridiculous aspects of the film wouldn't matter if the characters were believable, but because they are not we are left with a series of fast moving puzzles - it's all about timing and positioning like those old video games where you jump from one platform to another while the clock ticks.<br /><br />It's not surprising that some people love this film and others do not.  MI-GP does whiz-bang action better than anything I've seen to date, and if that's enough for you then this is your film.  If, like me, you need more than that then it will disappoint.  Just be clear on which camp you're in and all will be well :-)

B005VR91UW|5.0|Fifty-five years after its initial release, Little Richard's debut LP resounds with the primordial fire of rhythm `n' blues' jump to rock `n' roll. Richard took everything up a notch - the tempos, the innuendo and above all, the volume and energy of his vocals. Recorded primarily at New Orleans' legendary J&M studios, Richard was backed by the cream of the Crescent City's musicians, including Lee Allen, Alvin Taylor, Frank Fields and Earl Palmer. Though the same crew could be heard on other artists' records, with Richard in the lead, they heated up their New Orleans boogie-woogie as on few other sessions. There's a level of fervor, abandon and outrageousness in both Richard's singing and piano playing that none of his fellow founders could match.<br /><br />The original dozen tracks clock in at just over 28 minutes, but it's 28 minutes of killer rock `n' roll, with zero filler. The first hits were \\"Tutti Frutti,\\" \\"Long Tall Sally,\\" \\"Slippin' and Slidin',\\" \\"Rip it Up,\\" \\"Ready Teddy\\" and \\"She's Got It.\\" Three more - \\"Jenny Jenny,\\" \\"Miss Ann\\" and \\"True Fine Mama\\" - charted in '57 and '58. That leaves only three that didn't chart - \\"Can't Believe You Wanna Leave,\\" \\"Baby\\" and \\"Oh Why?\\" - each of which has the same incendiary spark of the better known singles. The CD reissue adds three audio tracks and two videos. The audio includes Richard's two original audition tracks and a previously unreleased interview with Specialty Records founder Art Rupe. Rupe talks about the audition tape, Richard's persistence at getting signed, the New Orleans sessions, the impact of \\"Tutti Frutti\\" and the on-again, off-again career it created.<br /><br />The audition tracks - Little Richard originals \\"Baby\\" and \\"All Night Long\\" - are surprising for their lack of indication of what was to come. Richard sang straight blues, with the band subdued behind him, not even hinting at the rock `n' roll mayhem he'd bring to his Specialty sessions. Rupe, looking for a B.B. King-type singer, heard something he liked, but had no idea what he was really getting. The videos are color screen tests (for [[ASIN:B000FKO3US The Girl Can't Help It]]) of Richard lip-synching \\"Tutti Frutti\\" and \\"Long Tall Sally,\\" highlighted visually by his swanky suits, awesome pompadour, pencil-thin moustache and his uninhibited dancing in the instrumental breaks. The set's 24-page booklet includes photos, the album's original liner notes, new notes by Lee Hildebrand, and a poster of the album cover. Rock `n' roll stars simply didn't shine any brighter than this. [2012 Hyperbolium]ing he liked, but had no idea what he was really getting.
